### File: `src\watcher.rs`

- Size: 12152 bytes
- Modified: SystemTime { intervals: 134205779471110313 }

```rust
   1 | use crate::error::{FlashError, Result};
   2 | use crate::indexer::IndexManager;
   3 | use crate::metadata::MetadataDb;
   4 | use crate::parsers::parse_file;
   5 | use blake3;
   6 | use notify::{Event, EventKind, RecommendedWatcher, RecursiveMode, Watcher};
   7 | use std::collections::HashMap;
   8 | use std::path::{Path, PathBuf};
   9 | use std::sync::Arc;
  10 | use std::time::Duration;
  11 | use tokio::sync::mpsc;
  12 | use tracing::{error, info, warn};
  13 | 
  14 | #[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
  15 | pub enum WatcherAction {
  16 |     Index,
  17 |     Remove,
  18 | }
  19 | 
  20 | /// Manages active file system watching with debouncing
  21 | pub struct WatcherManager {
  22 |     watchers: HashMap<String, RecommendedWatcher>,
  23 |     _indexer: Arc<IndexManager>,
  24 |     _metadata_db: Arc<MetadataDb>,
  25 |     _runtime_handle: tokio::runtime::Handle,
  26 |     external_tx: mpsc::Sender<(PathBuf, WatcherAction)>,
  27 | }
  28 | 
  29 | impl WatcherManager {
  30 |     /// Creates a new `WatcherManager`
  31 |     ///
  32 |     /// # Panics
  33 |     ///
  34 |     /// Panics if the background processor task fails to spawn.
  35 |     pub fn new(
  36 |         indexer: Arc<IndexManager>,
  37 |         metadata_db: Arc<MetadataDb>,
  38 |         allowed_extensions: std::collections::HashSet<String>,
  39 |     ) -> Self {
  40 |         let (external_tx, external_rx) = mpsc::channel::<(PathBuf, WatcherAction)>(1000);
  41 |         let runtime_handle = tokio::runtime::Handle::current();
  42 | 
  43 |         // Spawn background processor for debounced events
  44 |         Self::spawn_processor_task(
  45 |             &runtime_handle,
  46 |             external_rx,
  47 |             indexer.clone(),
  48 |             metadata_db.clone(),
  49 |             allowed_extensions,
  50 |         );
  51 | 
  52 |         Self {
  53 |             watchers: HashMap::new(),
  54 |             _indexer: indexer,
  55 |             _metadata_db: metadata_db,
  56 |             _runtime_handle: runtime_handle,
  57 |             external_tx,
  58 |         }
  59 |     }
  60 | 
  61 |     fn spawn_processor_task(
  62 |         runtime_handle: &tokio::runtime::Handle,
  63 |         mut external_rx: mpsc::Receiver<(PathBuf, WatcherAction)>,
  64 |         indexer: Arc<IndexManager>,
  65 |         metadata_db: Arc<MetadataDb>,
  66 |         allowed_extensions: std::collections::HashSet<String>,
  67 |     ) {
  68 |         const MAX_DEBOUNCE_WAIT: Duration = Duration::from_secs(5);
  69 |         const DEBOUNCE_GAP: Duration = Duration::from_millis(500);
  70 | 
  71 |         runtime_handle.spawn(async move {
  72 |             let mut buffer = HashMap::new();
  73 |             let mut first_event_time: Option<std::time::Instant> = None;
  74 | 
  75 |             loop {
  76 |                 let timeout_duration = first_event_time.map_or_else(
  77 |                     || Duration::from_secs(3600),
  78 |                     |first_time| {
  79 |                         let elapsed = first_time.elapsed();
  80 |                         if elapsed >= MAX_DEBOUNCE_WAIT {
  81 |                             Duration::from_millis(0) // Force flush immediately
  82 |                         } else {
  83 |                             DEBOUNCE_GAP.min(MAX_DEBOUNCE_WAIT.checked_sub(elapsed).unwrap())
  84 |                         }
  85 |                     },
  86 |                 );
  87 | 
  88 |                 tokio::select! {
  89 |                     res = external_rx.recv() => {
  90 |                         if let Some((path, action)) = res {
  91 |                             if buffer.is_empty() {
  92 |                                 first_event_time = Some(std::time::Instant::now());
  93 |                             }
  94 |                             buffer.insert(path, action);
  95 |                         } else {
  96 |                             break;
  97 |                         }
  98 |                     }
  99 |                     () = tokio::time::sleep(timeout_duration) => {
 100 |                         if buffer.is_empty() {
 101 |                             continue;
 102 |                         }
 103 |                         first_event_time = None;
 104 |                         let events = std::mem::take(&mut buffer);
 105 |                         Self::process_events(events, &indexer, &metadata_db, &allowed_extensions).await;
 106 |                     }
 107 |                 }
 108 |             }
 109 |         });
 110 |     }
 111 | 
 112 |     async fn process_events(
 113 |         events: HashMap<PathBuf, WatcherAction>,
 114 |         indexer: &Arc<IndexManager>,
 115 |         metadata_db: &Arc<MetadataDb>,
 116 |         allowed_extensions: &std::collections::HashSet<String>,
 117 |     ) {
 118 |         let mut needs_commit = false;
 119 | 
 120 |         // First pass: collect all paths that need to be removed
 121 |         let remove_paths: Vec<PathBuf> = events
 122 |             .iter()
 123 |             .filter(|(_, action)| matches!(action, WatcherAction::Remove))
 124 |             .map(|(path, _)| path.clone())
 125 |             .collect();
 126 | 
 127 |         // Second pass: collect all paths that need to be indexed
 128 |         let index_paths: Vec<PathBuf> = events
 129 |             .iter()
 130 |             .filter(|(_, action)| matches!(action, WatcherAction::Index))
 131 |             .map(|(path, _)| path.clone())
 132 |             .collect();
 133 | 
 134 |         // Process removes first
 135 |         for path in remove_paths {
 136 |             let path_str = path.to_string_lossy();
 137 |             let _ = indexer.remove_document(&path_str);
 138 |             if matches!(metadata_db.remove_file(&path), Ok(true)) {
 139 |                 needs_commit = true;
 140 |                 info!("Removed file (watcher): {:?}", path);
 141 |             }
 142 |         }
 143 | 
 144 |         // Then process indexes
 145 |         let mut docs_to_add = Vec::new();
 146 |         let mut meta_to_update = Vec::new();
 147 | 
 148 |         for path in index_paths {
 149 |             if let Some(ext) = path.extension().and_then(|e| e.to_str()) {
 150 |                 if !allowed_extensions.contains(&ext.to_lowercase()) {
 151 |                     continue;
 152 |                 }
 153 |             } else {
 154 |                 continue;
 155 |             }
 156 | 
 157 |             match Self::reindex_single_file(&path, metadata_db).await {
 158 |                 Ok(Some((doc, modified, size, hash))) => {
 159 |                     meta_to_update.push((doc.path.clone(), modified, size, hash));
 160 |                     docs_to_add.push((doc, modified, size));
 161 |                 }
 162 |                 Ok(None) => {} // Skipped
 163 |                 Err(e) => error!("Watcher error indexing {:?}: {}", path, e),
 164 |             }
 165 |         }
 166 | 
 167 |         if !docs_to_add.is_empty() {
 168 |             let _ = indexer.add_documents_batch(&docs_to_add);
 169 |             let _ = metadata_db.batch_update_metadata(&meta_to_update);
 170 |             needs_commit = true;
 171 |         }
 172 | 
 173 |         if needs_commit {
 174 |             if let Err(e) = indexer.commit() {
 175 |                 error!("Watcher failed to commit index: {}", e);
 176 |             } else {
 177 |                 indexer.invalidate_cache();
 178 |             }
 179 |         }
 180 |     }
 181 | 
 182 |     /// Get a sender to push external events (like USN Journal) into the watcher
 183 |     #[must_use]
 184 |     pub fn event_tx(&self) -> mpsc::Sender<(PathBuf, WatcherAction)> {
 185 |         self.external_tx.clone()
 186 |     }
 187 | 
 188 |     /// Update the list of watched directories
 189 |     pub fn update_watch_list(&mut self, dirs: &[String]) -> Result<()> {
 190 |         let current_dirs: std::collections::HashSet<String> = dirs.iter().cloned().collect();
 191 |         let existing_dirs: std::collections::HashSet<String> =
 192 |             self.watchers.keys().cloned().collect();
 193 | 
 194 |         // Remove watchers for directories no longer in the list
 195 |         for dir in existing_dirs.difference(&current_dirs) {
 196 |             self.watchers.remove(dir);
 197 |         }
 198 | 
 199 |         // Add watchers for new directories
 200 |         for dir in current_dirs.difference(&existing_dirs) {
 201 |             let tx = self.external_tx.clone();
 202 |             let mut watcher = notify::recommended_watcher(move |res: notify::Result<Event>| {
 203 |                 if let Ok(event) = res {
 204 |                     match event.kind {
 205 |                         EventKind::Modify(_) | EventKind::Create(_) | EventKind::Remove(_) => {
 206 |                             for path in &event.paths {
 207 |                                 let action = match event.kind {
 208 |                                     EventKind::Remove(_) => WatcherAction::Remove,
 209 |                                     _ => WatcherAction::Index,
 210 |                                 };
 211 |                                 let _ = tx.try_send((path.clone(), action));
 212 |                             }
 213 |                         }
 214 |                         _ => {}
 215 |                     }
 216 |                 }
 217 |             })
 218 |             .map_err(|e| FlashError::Io(std::sync::Arc::new(std::io::Error::other(e))))?;
 219 | 
 220 |             let path = Path::new(dir);
 221 |             if path.exists() {
 222 |                 watcher
 223 |                     .watch(path, RecursiveMode::Recursive)
 224 |                     .map_err(|e| FlashError::Io(std::sync::Arc::new(std::io::Error::other(e))))?;
 225 |                 self.watchers.insert(dir.clone(), watcher);
 226 |             }
 227 |         }
 228 | 
 229 |         Ok(())
 230 |     }
 231 | 
 232 |     // Returns parsed document data if file needs re-indexing
 233 |     async fn reindex_single_file(
 234 |         path: &Path,
 235 |         metadata_db: &Arc<MetadataDb>,
 236 |     ) -> Result<Option<(crate::parsers::ParsedDocument, u64, u64, [u8; 32])>> {
 237 |         if !path.exists() {
 238 |             return Ok(None);
 239 |         }
 240 | 
 241 |         let Ok(metadata) = std::fs::metadata(path) else {
 242 |             return Ok(None); // Ignore if cannot read metadata
 243 |         };
 244 | 
 245 |         let modified = metadata
 246 |             .modified()
 247 |             .unwrap_or(std::time::SystemTime::UNIX_EPOCH)
 248 |             .duration_since(std::time::SystemTime::UNIX_EPOCH)
 249 |             .unwrap_or_default()
 250 |             .as_secs();
 251 |         let size = metadata.len();
 252 | 
 253 |         // Skip check? If watcher said it changed, it probably did.
 254 |         // But checking db saves re-hashing if it was a false alarm.
 255 |         if !metadata_db
 256 |             .needs_reindex(path, modified, size)
 257 |             .unwrap_or(true)
 258 |         {
 259 |             return Ok(None);
 260 |         }
 261 | 
 262 |         let path_buf = path.to_path_buf();
 263 |         let parsed_res = tokio::task::spawn_blocking(move || parse_file(&path_buf))
 264 |             .await
 265 |             .map_err(|e| FlashError::parse(path, format!("Parse task failed: {e}")))?;
 266 | 
 267 |         let parsed = match parsed_res {
 268 |             Ok(p) => p,
 269 |             Err(e) => {
 270 |                 warn!("Failed to parse file {:?}: {}", path, e);
 271 |                 return Ok(None);
 272 |             }
 273 |         };
 274 | 
 275 |         let content_hash: [u8; 32] = blake3::hash(parsed.content.as_bytes()).into();
 276 | 
 277 |         Ok(Some((parsed, modified, size, content_hash)))
 278 |     }
 279 | }
 280 |

 322 |         writeln!(file, "Initial content").unwrap();
 323 |

 325 |         let result = WatcherManager::reindex_single_file(&file_path, &metadata).await;
 326 |         assert!(result.is_ok());
 327 |         let option = result.unwrap();
 328 |         assert!(option.is_some());
 329 |         let (doc, modified, size, _hash) = option.unwrap();
 330 |         assert_eq!(doc.content, "Initial content");
 331 | 
 332 |         metadata
 333 |             .update_metadata(&file_path, modified, size, [0; 32])
 334 |             .unwrap();
 335 | 
 336 |         // Should return None if no change
 337 |         let result = WatcherManager::reindex_single_file(&file_path, &metadata).await;
 338 |         assert!(result.is_ok());
 339 |         assert!(result.unwrap().is_none());
 340 |     }

   1 | use flash_search::error::Result;

   3 | use flash_search::{indexer::IndexManager, metadata::MetadataDb};
   4 | use std::fs;

   6 | use tempfile::tempdir;
   7 | 
   8 | #[tokio::test]
   9 | async fn test_end_to_end_search() -> Result<()> {
  10 |     let temp_workspace = tempdir()?;
  11 |     let index_dir = temp_workspace.path().join("index");
  12 |     let data_dir = temp_workspace.path().join("data");
  13 |     let settings_dir = temp_workspace.path().join("settings");
  14 |

  17 |     fs::create_dir_all(&settings_dir)?;
  18 |

  20 |     fs::write(&txt_path, "This is a unique test string for searching.")?;
  21 | 
  22 |     let md_path = data_dir.join("notes.md");
  23 |     fs::write(
  24 |         &md_path,
  25 |         "# Notes\n\nSome markdown content with unique keyword: flashsearchintegrationtest",
  26 |     )?;
  27 | 
  28 |     let indexer = Arc::new(IndexManager::open(&index_dir, 100)?);
  29 |     let metadata_db_path = index_dir.join("metadata.redb");
  30 |     let _metadata_db = Arc::new(MetadataDb::open(&metadata_db_path)?);
  31 | 
  32 |     let txt_path_clone = txt_path.clone();
  33 |     let md_path_clone = md_path.clone();

  35 |     let txt_doc =
  36 |         tokio::task::spawn_blocking(move || flash_search::parsers::parse_file(&txt_path_clone))
  37 |             .await
  38 |             .map_err(|e| flash_search::error::FlashError::parse(&txt_path, e.to_string()))??;
  39 | 
  40 |     let md_doc =
  41 |         tokio::task::spawn_blocking(move || flash_search::parsers::parse_file(&md_path_clone))
  42 |             .await
  43 |             .map_err(|e| flash_search::error::FlashError::parse(&md_path, e.to_string()))??;
  44 | 
  45 |     let now = std::time::SystemTime::now()
  46 |         .duration_since(std::time::UNIX_EPOCH)
  47 |         .unwrap()
  48 |         .as_secs();
  49 | 
  50 |     indexer.add_document(&txt_doc, now, 100)?;
  51 |     indexer.add_document(&md_doc, now, 200)?;
  52 |     indexer.commit()?;
  53 | 
  54 |     // Wait for indexing to complete - 500ms might be too short on some systems
  55 |     std::thread::sleep(std::time::Duration::from_millis(1500));
  56 | 
  57 |     let results = indexer
  58 |         .search(
  59 |             SearchParams::builder()
  60 |                 .query("unique test string")
  61 |                 .limit(10)
  62 |                 .case_sensitive(false)
  63 |                 .build(),
  64 |         )
  65 |         .await?;
  66 |     assert_eq!(results.len(), 1);
  67 |     assert!(results[0].file_path.contains("hello.txt"));
  68 | 
  69 |     let results = indexer
  70 |         .search(
  71 |             SearchParams::builder()
  72 |                 .query("flashsearchintegrationtest")
  73 |                 .limit(10)
  74 |                 .case_sensitive(false)
  75 |                 .build(),
  76 |         )
  77 |         .await?;
  78 |     assert_eq!(results.len(), 1);
  79 |     assert!(results[0].file_path.contains("notes.md"));
  80 | 
  81 |     Ok(())
  82 | }
```

   1 | # Third-Party Licenses

   4 | 
   5 | ## Core Dependencies
   6 | 
   7 | | Library | Purpose | License |
   8 | |---------|---------|---------|
   9 | | [Slint](https://slint.dev/) | GUI Framework | GPL-3.0 / Apache-2.0 |
  10 | | [Tantivy](https://github.com/quickwit-oss/tantivy) | Search Engine | MIT |
  11 | | [redb](https://github.com/cberner/redb) | Metadata Database | MIT / Apache-2.0 |
  12 | | [Tokio](https://tokio.rs/) | Async Runtime | MIT |
  13 | | [Rayon](https://github.com/rayon-rs/rayon) | Data Parallelism | MIT / Apache-2.0 |
  14 | | [quick-xml](https://github.com/tafia/quick-xml) | XML Parsing | MIT |
  15 | | [zip-rs](https://github.com/zip-rs/zip) | ZIP Extraction | MIT |
  16 | | [pdf-extract](https://github.com/jrmuizel/pdf-extract) | PDF Parsing | MIT |
  17 | | [memmap2](https://github.com/RazrFalcon/memmap2-rs) | Memory Mapping | MIT / Apache-2.0 |
  18 | | [blake3](https://github.com/BLAKE3-team/BLAKE3) | Hashing | CC0-1.0 / Apache-2.0 |
  19 | | [mimalloc](https://github.com/microsoft/mimalloc) | Memory Allocator | MIT |
  20 | 
  21 | ## Other Dependencies
  22 | 
  23 | Most other utilities used (e.g., `anyhow`, `thiserror`, `chrono`, `walkdir`, `regex`, `arboard`, `opener`, `rfd`) are licensed under either **MIT** or **Apache-2.0**.

### File: `agents.md`

- Size: 24944 bytes

```markdown
   1 | # AGENTS.md - AI Coding Agent Instructions
   2 | 
   3 | ## Project Overview
   4 | 
   5 | **Flash Search** is an ultrafast local full-text search application built purely with Rust. This document provides comprehensive instructions for AI coding agents working on this codebase.
   6 | 
   7 | ## Architecture Overview
   8 | 
   9 | ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
  10 | │                     Flash Search                             │
  11 | ├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  12 | │  UI (Iced)                                                  │
  13 | │  ├── iced_ui/       - High-performance GUI components       │
  14 | │  ├── search.rs      - Search view and logic bindings        │
  15 | │  └── settings.rs    - Settings view and logic bindings      │
  16 | ├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  17 | │  Rust Backend (Glue & Logic)                                │
  18 | │  ├── commands/      - Business logic handlers               │
  19 | │  └── state/         - Application state management          │
  20 | ├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
  21 | │  Core Engine                                                │
  22 | │  ├── indexer/       - Tantivy search engine wrapper         │
  23 | │  ├── parsers/       - Kreuzberg unified document intell.      │
  24 | │  ├── scanner/       - File system crawler                   │
  25 | │  └── metadata/      - redb database operations              │
  26 | └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
  27 | 
  28 | ## Project Structure
  29 | 
  30 | ```
  31 | flash-search/
  32 | ├── src/
  33 | │   ├── main.rs              # Application entry point
  34 | │   ├── lib.rs               # Library exports
  35 | │   ├── error.rs             # Error types
  36 | │   ├── models.rs            # Data models
  37 | │   ├── settings.rs          # Settings management
  38 | │   ├── commands/            # Business logic (AppState)
  39 | │   ├── iced_ui/             # Iced UI implementation
  40 | │   │   ├── mod.rs           # UI entry and core state
  41 | │   │   ├── search.rs        # Search screen UI
  42 | │   │   └── settings.rs      # Settings screen UI
  43 | │   ├── parsers/
  44 | │   │   ├── mod.rs           # Unified parser (via Kreuzberg)
  45 | │   │   └── memory_map.rs    # Mmap utilities
  46 | │   ├── indexer/
  47 | │   │   ├── mod.rs           # Indexer module
  48 | │   │   ├── schema.rs        # Tantivy schema
  49 | │   │   └── searcher.rs      # Query execution
  50 | │   └── metadata/
  51 | │       ├── mod.rs           # Metadata DB interface
  52 | │       └── db.rs            # redb definitions
  53 | ├── Cargo.toml               # Project dependencies
  54 | └── README.md
  55 | ```
  56 | 
  57 | ## Critical Implementation Guidelines
  58 | 
  59 | ### 1. Performance First
  60 | 
  61 | **This project prioritizes performance over convenience.**
  62 | 
  63 | - **Memory**: Keep RAM usage under 30MB at idle
  64 | - **Speed**: Search results must return in <50ms
  65 | - **I/O**: Use memory-mapped files for parsing
  66 | - **UI Responsiveness**: Never block the Iced event loop
  67 | 
  68 | **DON'Ts:**
  69 | - Don't perform heavy computations in Iced `update` methods (use `Command::perform` or `tokio::spawn`)
  70 | - Don't load large datasets into the UI at once (use pagination or lazy loading if needed)
  71 | 
  72 | ### 2. Error Handling
  73 | 
  74 | Use `anyhow` for error propagation and `thiserror` for custom error types:
  75 | 
  76 | ```rust
  77 | // Good
  78 | use anyhow::{Context, Result};
  79 | 
  80 | pub fn parse_file(path: &Path) -> Result<String> {
  81 |     let content = std::fs::read_to_string(path)
  82 |         .with_context(|| format!("Failed to read file: {}", path.display()))?;
  83 |     Ok(content)
  84 | }
  85 | 
  86 | // Custom errors for specific failure modes
  87 | #[derive(Error, Debug)]
  88 | pub enum ParseError {
  89 |     #[error("Unsupported file format: {0}")]
  90 |     UnsupportedFormat(String),
  91 |     #[error("File corrupted or encrypted")]
  92 |     CorruptedFile,
  93 |     #[error("IO error: {0}")]
  94 |     Io(#[from] std::io::Error),
  95 | }
  96 | ```
  97 | 
  98 | ### 3. Concurrency Model
  99 | 
 100 | ```rust
 101 | // File watching (async I/O) -> Tokio
 102 | // File parsing (CPU-bound) -> Rayon
 103 | // Search queries -> Tantivy (already parallel)
 104 | 
 105 | // Example: Hybrid approach
 106 | use rayon::prelude::*;
 107 | use tokio::task;
 108 | 
 109 | pub async fn index_directory(path: PathBuf) -> Result<()> {
 110 |     // Walk directory (async I/O)
 111 |     let files = walk_directory(&path).await?;
 112 |     
 113 |     // Parse files in parallel (CPU-bound)
 114 |     let results: Vec<_> = files
 115 |         .par_iter()
 116 |         .map(|file| parse_file(file))
 117 |         .collect();
 118 |     
 119 |     Ok(())
 120 | }
 121 | ```
 122 | 
 123 | ### 4. Parser Implementation (Unified via Kreuzberg)
 124 | 
 125 | ```rust
 126 | pub fn parse_file(path: &Path) -> Result<ParsedDocument> {
 127 |     // Kreuzberg handles 75+ formats automatically
 128 |     let result = kreuzberg::extract_file_sync(path)
 129 |         .map_err(|e| FlashError::parse(path, format!("Extraction failed: {}", e)))?;
 130 | 
 131 |     Ok(ParsedDocument {
 132 |         path: path.to_string_lossy().to_string(),
 133 |         content: result.content,
 134 |         title: result.metadata.title,
 135 |     })
 136 | }
 137 | ```
 138 | 
 139 | ### 5. Tantivy Schema
 140 | 
 141 | ```rust
 142 | use tantivy::schema::*;
 143 | 
 144 | pub fn create_schema() -> Schema {
 145 |     let mut schema_builder = Schema::builder();
 146 |     
 147 |     // Store file path for retrieval
 148 |     schema_builder.add_text_field(
 149 |         "file_path",
 150 |         STRING | STORED
 151 |     );
 152 |     
 153 |     // Index content but don't store (retrieved from disk on demand)
 154 |     let text_options = TextOptions::default()
 155 |         .set_indexing_options(
 156 |             TextFieldIndexing::default()
 157 |                 .set_tokenizer("default")
 158 |                 .set_index_option(IndexRecordOption::WithFreqsAndPositions)
 159 |         )
 160 |         .set_stored(false);
 161 |     schema_builder.add_text_field("content", text_options);
 162 |     
 163 |     // Store title for display
 164 |     schema_builder.add_text_field(
 165 |         "title",
 166 |         TEXT | STORED
 167 |     );
 168 |     
 169 |     // Index timestamp for sorting
 170 |     schema_builder.add_date_field(
 171 |         "modified",
 172 |         FAST | INDEXED
 173 |     );
 174 |     
 175 |     schema_builder.build()
 176 | }
 177 | ```
 178 | 
 179 | ### 6. Metadata Database (redb)
 180 | 
 181 | ```rust
 182 | use redb::{Database, TableDefinition};
 183 | 
 184 | const FILES_TABLE: TableDefinition<&str, FileMetadata> = TableDefinition::new("files");
 185 | 
 186 | #[derive(Debug, Clone, serde::Serialize, serde::Deserialize)]
 187 | pub struct FileMetadata {
 188 |     pub path: String,
 189 |     pub modified: u64,      // Unix timestamp
 190 |     pub size: u64,
 191 |     pub content_hash: [u8; 32], // blake3 hash
 192 |     pub indexed_at: u64,
 193 | }
 194 | 
 195 | pub struct MetadataDb {
 196 |     db: Database,
 197 | }
 198 | 
 199 | impl MetadataDb {
 200 |     pub fn needs_reindex(&self, path: &Path, modified: u64) -> Result<bool> {
 201 |         let txn = self.db.begin_read()?;
 202 |         let table = txn.open_table(FILES_TABLE)?;
 203 |         
 204 |         match table.get(path.to_str().unwrap())? {
 205 |             Some(metadata) => {
 206 |                 let meta = metadata.value();
 207 |                 Ok(meta.modified != modified)
 208 |             }
 209 |             None => Ok(true), // File not indexed yet
 210 |         }
 211 |     }
 212 | }
 213 | ```
 214 | 
 215 | ### 7. Iced Integration (UI Glue)
 216 | 
 217 | ```rust
 218 | use iced::{Application, Command, Element};
 219 | 
 220 | pub struct SearchApp {
 221 |     state: Arc<AppState>,
 222 |     search_query: String,
 223 |     results: Vec<FileItem>,
 224 | }
 225 | 
 226 | #[derive(Debug, Clone)]
 227 | pub enum Message {
 228 |     SearchInputChanged(String),
 229 |     PerformSearch,
 230 |     SearchResultsReceived(Vec<FileItem>),
 231 | }
 232 | 
 233 | impl Application for SearchApp {
 234 |     type Message = Message;
 235 |     // ...
 236 | 
 237 |     fn update(&mut self, message: Message) -> Command<Message> {
 238 |         match message {
 239 |             Message::SearchInputChanged(query) => {
 240 |                 self.search_query = query;
 241 |                 Command::none()
 242 |             }
 243 |             Message::PerformSearch => {
 244 |                 let state = self.state.clone();
 245 |                 let query = self.search_query.clone();
 246 |                 
 247 |                 // Offload search to async command
 248 |                 Command::perform(async move {
 249 |                     let results = state.indexer.search(&query).await.unwrap_or_default();
 250 |                     results.into_iter().map(FileItem::from).collect()
 251 |                 }, Message::SearchResultsReceived)
 252 |             }
 253 |             Message::SearchResultsReceived(results) => {
 254 |                 self.results = results;
 255 |                 Command::none()
 256 |             }
 257 |         }
 258 |     }
 259 | 
 260 |     fn view(&self) -> Element<Message> {
 261 |         // ... Iced view layout construction ...
 262 |         iced::widget::text("Search View").into()
 263 |     }
 264 | }
 265 | ```
 266 | 
 267 | ### 8. Iced Component Patterns
 268 | 
 269 | Follow the standard Elm architecture when creating view components in Iced. Keep state isolated where appropriate and fire clear descriptive messages.
 270 | 
 271 | ## Common Tasks
 272 | 
 273 | ### Adding a New File Parser
 274 | 
 275 | 1. Create `src/parsers/<format>.rs`
 276 | 2. Implement `parse_<format>(path: &Path) -> Result<ParsedDocument>`
 277 | 3. Register in `src/parsers/mod.rs` dispatch function
 278 | 4. Add MIME type detection
 279 | 5. Write unit tests with sample files
 280 | 
 281 | ### Modifying the Search Schema
 282 | 
 283 | 1. Update `src/indexer/schema.rs`
 284 | 2. **WARNING**: Schema changes require reindexing all documents
 285 | 3. Consider migration strategy for existing users
 286 | 4. Bump index version in constants
 287 | 
 288 | ### Adding a New Iced Message
 289 | 
 290 | 1. Define the message variant in the relevant `Message` enum (e.g., in `src/iced_ui/mod.rs`)
 291 | 2. Handle the message in the `update()` function
 292 | 3. Return an async `Command::perform` for any IO/backend work
 293 | 4. Ensure the view triggers the matching message on user interactions
 294 | 
 295 | ## Testing Guidelines
 296 | 
 297 | ### Unit Tests (Rust)
 298 | 
 299 | ```rust
 300 | #[cfg(test)]
 301 | mod tests {
 302 |     use super::*;
 303 |     
 304 |     #[test]
 305 |     fn test_docx_parsing() {
 306 |         let doc = parse_docx(Path::new("tests/fixtures/sample.docx"))
 307 |             .expect("Should parse DOCX");
 308 |         
 309 |         assert!(doc.content.contains("Hello World"));
 310 |         assert_eq!(doc.title, Some("Sample Document".to_string()));
 311 |     }
 312 | }
 313 | ```
 314 | 
 315 | ### Integration Tests
 316 | 
 317 | - Test with large file collections (10K+ files)
 318 | - Measure memory usage with `valgrind` or `/usr/bin/time -v`
 319 | - Benchmark search latency with `cargo bench`
 320 | 
 321 | ## Build Commands
 322 | 
 323 | ```bash
 324 | # Build and Run
 325 | cargo run
 326 | 
 327 | # Build for production
 328 | cargo build --release
 329 | 
 330 | # Run Rust tests
 331 | cargo test
 332 | ```
 333 | 
 334 | ## Troubleshooting
 335 | 
 336 | ### High Memory Usage
 337 | 
 338 | - Check for memory leaks in parsers (ensure files are closed)
 339 | - Verify Tantivy index writer buffer size
 340 | - Profile with `heaptrack` or `dhat`
 341 | 
 342 | ### Slow Search
 343 | 
 344 | - Verify Tantivy reader is cached (don't recreate)
 345 | - Check if index is memory-mapped
 346 | - Profile with `perf` or `samply`
 347 | 
 348 | ### Parser Failures
 349 | 
 350 | - Check file encoding detection
 351 | - Verify zip/xml parsing handles malformed files gracefully
 352 | - Add more comprehensive error contexts
 353 | 
 354 | ## Resources
 355 | 
 356 | - [Iced Documentation](https://docs.rs/iced/latest/iced/)
 357 | - [Tantivy Documentation](https://docs.rs/tantivy/latest/tantivy/)
 358 | - [Redb Documentation](https://docs.rs/redb/latest/redb/)
 359 | - [Rayon Documentation](https://docs.rs/rayon/latest/rayon/)
 360 | 
 361 | ## Contact
 362 | 
 363 | For questions about implementation details, refer to:
 364 | - GitHub Issues: https://github.com/yourusername/flash-search/issues
 365 | - Architecture Decisions: See `docs/adr/` directory
 366 | 
 367 | ---
 368 | 
 369 | **Last Updated**: 2024
 370 | **Version**: 0.1.0
 371 | 
 372 | ## Self-Healing Rules
 373 | - On borrow checker errors: Scan stack trace, add explicit lifetimes ('a), clone owned data where safe, or refactor to Rc<RefCell<T>> / Arc<Mutex<T>> for shared state.
 374 | - Lifetime mismatches: Infer from context (e.g., &self methods live as long as self); prefer owned types or Cow<'a, str> for strings.
 375 | - Async pinning: Detect Pin<Box<dyn Future>> needs; unwrap with .await safely, use tokio::spawn for non-Send futures, or Box::pin(async move {}).
 376 | - Always: Run `cargo check --tests` + `cargo clippy --fix` after edits; iterate until zero warnings. If fails 3x, request human review.
 377 | - Disable browser verification: Set verify_browser: false for CLI/binary focus—no screenshots/UI tests.
 378 | 
 379 | <!-- desloppify-begin -->
 380 | <!-- desloppify-skill-version: 3 -->
 381 | ---
 382 | name: desloppify
 383 | description: >
 384 |   Codebase health scanner and technical debt tracker. Use when the user asks
 385 |   about code quality, technical debt, dead code, large files, god classes,
 386 |   duplicate functions, code smells, naming issues, import cycles, or coupling
 387 |   problems. Also use when asked for a health score, what to fix next, or to
 388 |   create a cleanup plan. Supports 28 languages.
 389 | allowed-tools: Bash(desloppify *)
 390 | ---
 391 | 
 392 | # Desloppify
 393 | 
 394 | ## 1. Your Job
 395 | 
 396 | Maximise the **strict score** honestly. Your main cycle: **scan → plan → execute → rescan**. Follow the scan output's **INSTRUCTIONS FOR AGENTS** — don't substitute your own analysis.
 397 | 
 398 | **Don't be lazy.** Do large refactors and small detailed fixes with equal energy. If it takes touching 20 files, touch 20 files. If it's a one-line change, make it. No task is too big or too small — fix things properly, not minimally.
 399 | 
 400 | ## 2. The Workflow
 401 | 
 402 | Three phases, repeated as a cycle.
 403 | 
 404 | ### Phase 1: Scan and review — understand the codebase
 405 | 
 406 | ```bash
 407 | desloppify scan --path .       # analyse the codebase
 408 | desloppify status              # check scores — are we at target?
 409 | ```
 410 | 
 411 | The scan will tell you if subjective dimensions need review. Follow its instructions. To trigger a review manually:
 412 | ```bash
 413 | desloppify review --prepare    # then follow your runner's review workflow
 414 | ```
 415 | 
 416 | ### Phase 2: Plan — decide what to work on
 417 | 
 418 | After reviews, triage stages and plan creation appear as queue items in `next`. Complete them in order:
 419 | ```bash
 420 | desloppify next                                        # shows the next workflow step
 421 | desloppify plan triage --stage observe --report "themes and root causes..."
 422 | desloppify plan triage --stage reflect --report "comparison against completed work..."
 423 | desloppify plan triage --stage organize --report "summary of priorities..."
 424 | desloppify plan triage --complete --strategy "execution plan..."
 425 | ```
 426 | 
 427 | Then shape the queue. **The plan shapes everything `next` gives you** — don't skip this step.
 428 | 
 429 | ```bash
 430 | desloppify plan                          # see the full ordered queue
 431 | desloppify plan reorder <pat> top        # reorder — what unblocks the most?
 432 | desloppify plan cluster create <name>    # group related issues to batch-fix
 433 | desloppify plan focus <cluster>          # scope next to one cluster
 434 | desloppify plan skip <pat>              # defer — hide from next
 435 | ```
 436 | 
 437 | More plan commands:
 438 | ```bash
 439 | desloppify plan reorder <cluster> top    # move all cluster members at once
 440 | desloppify plan reorder <a> <b> top     # mix clusters + findings in one reorder
 441 | desloppify plan reorder <pat> before -t X  # position relative to another item/cluster
 442 | desloppify plan cluster reorder a,b top # reorder multiple clusters as one block
 443 | desloppify plan resolve <pat>           # mark complete
 444 | desloppify plan reopen <pat>             # reopen
 445 | ```
 446 | 
 447 | ### Phase 3: Execute — grind the queue to completion
 448 | 
 449 | Trust the plan and execute. Don't rescan mid-queue — finish the queue first.
 450 | 
 451 | **Branch first.** Create a dedicated branch for health work — never commit directly to main:
 452 | ```bash
 453 | git checkout -b desloppify/code-health    # or desloppify/<focus-area>
 454 | ```
 455 | 
 456 | **Set up commit tracking.** If you have a PR, link it for auto-updated descriptions:
 457 | ```bash
 458 | desloppify config set commit_pr 42        # PR number for auto-updates
 459 | ```
 460 | 
 461 | **The loop:**
 462 | ```
 463 | 1. desloppify next              ← what to fix next
 464 | 2. Fix the issue in code
 465 | 3. Resolve it (next shows you the exact command including required attestation)
 466 | 4. When you have a logical batch, commit:
 467 |    git add <files> && git commit -m "desloppify: fix 3 deferred_import findings"
 468 | 5. Record the commit:
 469 |    desloppify plan commit-log record      # moves findings uncommitted → committed, updates PR
 470 | 6. Push periodically:
 471 |    git push -u origin desloppify/code-health
 472 | 7. Repeat until the queue is empty
 473 | ```
 474 | 
 475 | Score may temporarily drop after fixes — cascade effects are normal, keep going.
 476 | If `next` suggests an auto-fixer, run `desloppify autofix <fixer> --dry-run` to preview, then apply.
 477 | 
 478 | **When the queue is clear, go back to Phase 1.** New issues will surface, cascades will have resolved, priorities will have shifted. This is the cycle.
 479 | 
 480 | ### Other useful commands
 481 | 
 482 | ```bash
 483 | desloppify next --count 5                         # top 5 priorities
 484 | desloppify next --cluster <name>                  # drill into a cluster
 485 | desloppify show <pattern>                         # filter by file/detector/ID
 486 | desloppify show --status open                     # all open findings
 487 | desloppify plan skip --permanent "<id>" --note "reason" --attest "..." # accept debt
 488 | desloppify exclude <path>                         # exclude a directory from scanning
 489 | desloppify config show                            # show all config including excludes
 490 | desloppify scan --path . --reset-subjective       # reset subjective baseline to 0
 491 | ```
 492 | 
 493 | ## 3. Reference
 494 | 
 495 | ### How scoring works
 496 | 
 497 | Overall score = **40% mechanical** + **60% subjective**.
 498 | 
 499 | - **Mechanical (40%)**: auto-detected issues — duplication, dead code, smells, unused imports, security. Fixed by changing code and rescanning.
 500 | - **Subjective (60%)**: design quality review — naming, error handling, abstractions, clarity. Starts at **0%** until reviewed. The scan will prompt you when a review is needed.
 501 | - **Strict score** is the north star: wontfix items count as open. The gap between overall and strict is your wontfix debt.
 502 | - **Score types**: overall (lenient), strict (wontfix counts), objective (mechanical only), verified (confirmed fixes only).
 503 | 
 504 | ### Subjective reviews in detail
 505 | 
 506 | - **Local runner (Codex)**: `desloppify review --run-batches --runner codex --parallel --scan-after-import` — automated end-to-end.
 507 | - **Local runner (Claude)**: `desloppify review --prepare` → launch parallel subagents → `desloppify review --import merged.json` — see skill doc overlay for details.
 508 | - **Cloud/external**: `desloppify review --external-start --external-runner claude` → follow session template → `--external-submit`.
 509 | - **Manual path**: `desloppify review --prepare` → review per dimension → `desloppify review --import file.json`.
 510 | - Import first, fix after — import creates tracked state entries for correlation.
 511 | - Target-matching scores trigger auto-reset to prevent gaming.
 512 | - Even moderate scores (60-80) dramatically improve overall health.
 513 | - Stale dimensions auto-surface in `next` — just follow the queue.
 514 | 
 515 | ### Review output format
 516 | 
 517 | Return machine-readable JSON for review imports. For `--external-submit`, include `session` from the generated template:
 518 | 
 519 | ```json
 520 | {
 521 |   "session": {
 522 |     "id": "<session_id_from_template>",
 523 |     "token": "<session_token_from_template>"
 524 |   },
 525 |   "assessments": {
 526 |     "<dimension_from_query>": 0
 527 |   },
 528 |   "findings": [
 529 |     {
 530 |       "dimension": "<dimension_from_query>",
 531 |       "identifier": "short_id",
 532 |       "summary": "one-line defect summary",
 533 |       "related_files": ["relative/path/to/file.py"],
 534 |       "evidence": ["specific code observation"],
 535 |       "suggestion": "concrete fix recommendation",
 536 |       "confidence": "high|medium|low"
 537 |     }
 538 |   ]
 539 | }
 540 | ```
 541 | 
 542 | **Import rules:**
 543 | - `findings` MUST match `query.system_prompt` exactly (including `related_files`, `evidence`, and `suggestion`). Use `"findings": []` when no defects found.
 544 | - Import is fail-closed: invalid findings abort unless `--allow-partial` is passed.
 545 | - Assessment scores are auto-applied from trusted internal or cloud session imports. Legacy `--attested-external` remains supported.
 546 | 
 547 | **Import paths:**
 548 | - Robust session flow (recommended): `desloppify review --external-start --external-runner claude` → use generated prompt/template → run printed `--external-submit` command.
 549 | - Durable scored import (legacy): `desloppify review --import findings.json --attested-external --attest "I validated this review was completed without awareness of overall score and is unbiased."`
 550 | - Findings-only fallback: `desloppify review --import findings.json`
 551 | 
 552 | ### Review integrity
 553 | 
 554 | 1. Do not use prior chat context, score history, or target-threshold anchoring.
 555 | 2. Score from evidence only; when mixed, score lower and explain uncertainty.
 556 | 3. Assess every requested dimension; never drop one. If evidence is weak, score lower.
 557 | 
 558 | ### Reviewer agent prompt
 559 | 
 560 | Runners that support agent definitions (Cursor, Copilot, Gemini) can create a dedicated reviewer agent. Use this system prompt:
 561 | 
 562 | ```
 563 | You are a code quality reviewer. You will be given a codebase path, a set of
 564 | dimensions to score, and what each dimension means. Read the code, score each
 565 | dimension 0-100 from evidence only, and return JSON in the required format.
 566 | Do not anchor to target thresholds. When evidence is mixed, score lower and
 567 | explain uncertainty.
 568 | ```
 569 | 
 570 | See your editor's overlay section below for the agent config format.
 571 | 
 572 | ### Commit tracking & branch workflow
 573 | 
 574 | Work on a dedicated branch named `desloppify/<description>` (e.g., `desloppify/code-health`, `desloppify/fix-smells`). Never push health work directly to main.
 575 | 
 576 | ```bash
 577 | desloppify config set commit_pr 42              # link to your PR
 578 | desloppify plan commit-log                      # see uncommitted + committed status
 579 | desloppify plan commit-log record               # record HEAD commit, update PR description
 580 | desloppify plan commit-log record --note "why"  # with rationale
 581 | desloppify plan commit-log record --only "smells::*"  # record specific findings only
 582 | desloppify plan commit-log history              # show commit records
 583 | desloppify plan commit-log pr                   # preview PR body markdown
 584 | desloppify config set commit_tracking_enabled false  # disable guidance
 585 | ```
 586 | 
 587 | After resolving findings as `fixed`, the tool shows uncommitted work, committed history, and a suggested commit message. After committing externally, run `record` to move findings from uncommitted to committed and auto-update the linked PR description.
 588 | 
 589 | ### Key concepts
 590 | 
 591 | - **Tiers**: T1 auto-fix → T2 quick manual → T3 judgment call → T4 major refactor.
 592 | - **Auto-clusters**: related findings are auto-grouped in `next`. Drill in with `next --cluster <name>`.
 593 | - **Zones**: production/script (scored), test/config/generated/vendor (not scored). Fix with `zone set`.
 594 | - **Wontfix cost**: widens the lenient↔strict gap. Challenge past decisions when the gap grows.
 595 | - Score can temporarily drop after fixes (cascade effects are normal).
 596 | 
 597 | ## 4. Escalate Tool Issues Upstream
 598 | 
 599 | When desloppify itself appears wrong or inconsistent:
 600 | 
 601 | 1. Capture a minimal repro (`command`, `path`, `expected`, `actual`).
 602 | 2. Open a GitHub issue in `peteromallet/desloppify`.
 603 | 3. If you can fix it safely, open a PR linked to that issue.
 604 | 4. If unsure whether it is tool bug vs user workflow, issue first, PR second.
 605 | 
 606 | ## Prerequisite
 607 | 
 608 | `command -v desloppify >/dev/null 2>&1 && echo "desloppify: installed" || echo "NOT INSTALLED — run: pip install --upgrade git+https://github.com/peteromallet/desloppify.git"`
 609 | 
 610 | <!-- desloppify-end -->
 611 | 
 612 | ## Gemini CLI Overlay
 613 | 
 614 | Gemini CLI has experimental subagent support, but subagents currently run
 615 | sequentially (not in parallel). Review dimensions one at a time.
 616 | 
 617 | ### Setup
 618 | 
 619 | Enable subagents in Gemini CLI settings:
 620 | ```json
 621 | {
 622 |   "experimental": {
 623 |     "enableAgents": true
 624 |   }
 625 | }
 626 | ```
 627 | 
 628 | Optionally define a reviewer agent in `.gemini/agents/desloppify-reviewer.md`:
 629 | 
 630 | ```yaml
 631 | ---
 632 | name: desloppify-reviewer
 633 | description: Scores subjective codebase quality dimensions for desloppify
 634 | kind: local
 635 | tools:
 636 |   - read_file
 637 |   - search_code
 638 | temperature: 0.2
 639 | max_turns: 10
 640 | ---
 641 | ```
 642 | 
 643 | Use the prompt from the "Reviewer agent prompt" section above.
 644 | 
 645 | ### Review workflow
 646 | 
 647 | Invoke the reviewer agent for each group of dimensions sequentially.
 648 | Even without parallelism, isolating dimensions across separate agent
 649 | invocations prevents score bleed between concerns.
 650 | 
 651 | Merge assessments and findings, then import.
 652 | 
 653 | When Gemini CLI adds parallel subagent execution, split dimensions across
 654 | concurrent agent calls instead.
 655 | 
 656 | <!-- desloppify-overlay: gemini -->
 657 | <!-- desloppify-end -->
```

### File: `skills\kreuzberg\SKILL.md`

```markdown
   1 | ---
   2 | name: kreuzberg
   3 | description: >-
   4 |   Extract text, tables, metadata, and images from 91+ document formats
   5 |   (PDF, Office, images, HTML, email, archives, academic) using Kreuzberg.
   6 |   Use when writing code that calls Kreuzberg APIs in Python, Node.js/TypeScript,
   7 |   Rust, or CLI. Covers installation, extraction (sync/async), configuration
   8 |   (OCR, chunking, output format), batch processing, error handling, and plugins.
   9 | license: Elastic-2.0
  10 | metadata:
  11 |   author: kreuzberg-dev
  12 |   version: "1.0"
  13 |   repository: https://github.com/kreuzberg-dev/kreuzberg
  14 | ---
  15 | 
  16 | # Kreuzberg Document Extraction
  17 | 
  18 | Kreuzberg is a high-performance document intelligence library with a Rust core and native bindings for Python, Node.js/TypeScript, Ruby, Go, Java, C#, PHP, and Elixir. It extracts text, tables, metadata, and images from 91+ file formats including PDF, Office documents, images (with OCR), HTML, email, archives, and academic formats.
  19 | 
  20 | Use this skill when writing code that:
  21 | 
  22 | - Extracts text or metadata from documents
  23 | - Performs OCR on scanned documents or images
  24 | - Batch-processes multiple files
  25 | - Configures extraction options (output format, chunking, OCR, language detection)
  26 | - Implements custom plugins (post-processors, validators, OCR backends)
  27 | 
  28 | ## Installation
  29 | 
  30 | ### Python
  31 | 
  32 | ```bash
  33 | pip install kreuzberg
  34 | # Optional OCR backends:
  35 | pip install kreuzberg[easyocr]    # EasyOCR
  36 | pip install kreuzberg[paddleocr]  # PaddleOCR
  37 | ```
  38 | 
  39 | ### Node.js
  40 | 
  41 | ```bash
  42 | npm install @kreuzberg/node
  43 | ```
  44 | 
  45 | ### Rust
  46 | 
  47 | ```toml
  48 | # Cargo.toml
  49 | [dependencies]
  50 | kreuzberg = { version = "4", features = ["tokio-runtime"] }
  51 | # features: tokio-runtime (required for sync + batch), pdf, ocr, chunking,
  52 | #           embeddings, language-detection, keywords-yake, keywords-rake
  53 | ```
  54 | 
  55 | ### CLI
  56 | 
  57 | ```bash
  58 | # Download from GitHub releases, or:
  59 | cargo install kreuzberg-cli
  60 | ```
  61 | 
  62 | ## Quick Start
  63 | 
  64 | ### Python (Async)
  65 | 
  66 | ```python
  67 | from kreuzberg import extract_file
  68 | 
  69 | result = await extract_file("document.pdf")
  70 | print(result.content)       # extracted text
  71 | print(result.metadata)      # document metadata
  72 | print(result.tables)        # extracted tables
  73 | ```
  74 | 
  75 | ### Python (Sync)
  76 | 
  77 | ```python
  78 | from kreuzberg import extract_file_sync
  79 | 
  80 | result = extract_file_sync("document.pdf")
  81 | print(result.content)
  82 | ```
  83 | 
  84 | ### Node.js
  85 | 
  86 | ```typescript
  87 | import { extractFile } from '@kreuzberg/node';
  88 | 
  89 | const result = await extractFile('document.pdf');
  90 | console.log(result.content);
  91 | console.log(result.metadata);
  92 | console.log(result.tables);
  93 | ```
  94 | 
  95 | ### Node.js (Sync)
  96 | 
  97 | ```typescript
  98 | import { extractFileSync } from '@kreuzberg/node';
  99 | 
 100 | const result = extractFileSync('document.pdf');
 101 | ```
 102 | 
 103 | ### Rust (Async)
 104 | 
 105 | ```rust
 106 | use kreuzberg::{extract_file, ExtractionConfig};
 107 | 
 108 | #[tokio::main]
 109 | async fn main() -> kreuzberg::Result<()> {
 110 |     let config = ExtractionConfig::default();
 111 |     let result = extract_file("document.pdf", None, &config).await?;
 112 |     println!("{}", result.content);
 113 |     Ok(())
 114 | }
 115 | ```
 116 | 
 117 | ### Rust (Sync) — requires `tokio-runtime` feature
 118 | 
 119 | ```rust
 120 | use kreuzberg::{extract_file_sync, ExtractionConfig};
 121 | 
 122 | fn main() -> kreuzberg::Result<()> {
 123 |     let config = ExtractionConfig::default();
 124 |     let result = extract_file_sync("document.pdf", None, &config)?;
 125 |     println!("{}", result.content);
 126 |     Ok(())
 127 | }
 128 | ```
 129 | 
 130 | ### CLI
 131 | 
 132 | ```bash
 133 | kreuzberg extract document.pdf
 134 | kreuzberg extract document.pdf --format json
 135 | kreuzberg extract document.pdf --output-format markdown
 136 | ```
 137 | 
 138 | ## Configuration
 139 | 
 140 | All languages use the same configuration structure with language-appropriate naming conventions.
 141 | 
 142 | ### Python (snake_case)
 143 | 
 144 | ```python
 145 | from kreuzberg import (
 146 |     ExtractionConfig, OcrConfig, TesseractConfig,
 147 |     PdfConfig, ChunkingConfig,
 148 | )
 149 | 
 150 | config = ExtractionConfig(
 151 |     ocr=OcrConfig(
 152 |         backend="tesseract",
 153 |         language="eng",
 154 |         tesseract_config=TesseractConfig(psm=6, enable_table_detection=True),
 155 |     ),
 156 |     pdf_options=PdfConfig(passwords=["secret123"]),
 157 |     chunking=ChunkingConfig(max_chars=1000, max_overlap=200),
 158 |     output_format="markdown",
 159 | )
 160 | 
 161 | result = await extract_file("document.pdf", config=config)
 162 | ```
 163 | 
 164 | ### Node.js (camelCase)
 165 | 
 166 | ```typescript
 167 | import { extractFile, type ExtractionConfig } from '@kreuzberg/node';
 168 | 
 169 | const config: ExtractionConfig = {
 170 |     ocr: { backend: 'tesseract', language: 'eng' },
 171 |     pdfOptions: { passwords: ['secret123'] },
 172 |     chunking: { maxChars: 1000, maxOverlap: 200 },
 173 |     outputFormat: 'markdown',
 174 | };
 175 | 
 176 | const result = await extractFile('document.pdf', null, config);
 177 | ```
 178 | 
 179 | ### Rust (snake_case)
 180 | 
 181 | ```rust
 182 | use kreuzberg::{ExtractionConfig, OcrConfig, ChunkingConfig, OutputFormat};
 183 | 
 184 | let config = ExtractionConfig {
 185 |     ocr: Some(OcrConfig {
 186 |         backend: "tesseract".into(),
 187 |         language: "eng".into(),
 188 |         ..Default::default()
 189 |     }),
 190 |     chunking: Some(ChunkingConfig {
 191 |         max_characters: 1000,
 192 |         overlap: 200,
 193 |         ..Default::default()
 194 |     }),
 195 |     output_format: OutputFormat::Markdown,
 196 |     ..Default::default()
 197 | };
 198 | 
 199 | let result = extract_file("document.pdf", None, &config).await?;
 200 | ```
 201 | 
 202 | ### Config File (TOML)
 203 | 
 204 | ```toml
 205 | output_format = "markdown"
 206 | 
 207 | [ocr]
 208 | backend = "tesseract"
 209 | language = "eng"
 210 | 
 211 | [chunking]
 212 | max_chars = 1000
 213 | max_overlap = 200
 214 | 
 215 | [pdf_options]
 216 | passwords = ["secret123"]
 217 | ```
 218 | 
 219 | ```bash
 220 | # CLI: auto-discovers kreuzberg.toml in current/parent directories
 221 | kreuzberg extract doc.pdf
 222 | # or explicit:
 223 | kreuzberg extract doc.pdf --config kreuzberg.toml
 224 | kreuzberg extract doc.pdf --config-json '{"ocr":{"backend":"tesseract","language":"deu"}}'
 225 | ```
 226 | 
 227 | ## Batch Processing
 228 | 
 229 | ### Python
 230 | 
 231 | ```python
 232 | from kreuzberg import batch_extract_files, batch_extract_files_sync
 233 | 
 234 | # Async
 235 | results = await batch_extract_files(["doc1.pdf", "doc2.docx", "doc3.xlsx"])
 236 | 
 237 | # Sync
 238 | results = batch_extract_files_sync(["doc1.pdf", "doc2.docx"])
 239 | 
 240 | for result in results:
 241 |     print(f"{len(result.content)} chars extracted")
 242 | ```
 243 | 
 244 | ### Node.js
 245 | 
 246 | ```typescript
 247 | import { batchExtractFiles } from '@kreuzberg/node';
 248 | 
 249 | const results = await batchExtractFiles(['doc1.pdf', 'doc2.docx']);
 250 | ```
 251 | 
 252 | ### Rust — requires `tokio-runtime` feature
 253 | 
 254 | ```rust
 255 | use kreuzberg::{batch_extract_file, ExtractionConfig};
 256 | 
 257 | let config = ExtractionConfig::default();
 258 | let paths = vec!["doc1.pdf", "doc2.docx"];
 259 | let results = batch_extract_file(paths, &config).await?;
 260 | ```
 261 | 
 262 | ### CLI
 263 | 
 264 | ```bash
 265 | kreuzberg batch *.pdf --format json
 266 | kreuzberg batch docs/*.docx --output-format markdown
 267 | ```
 268 | 
 269 | ## OCR
 270 | 
 271 | OCR runs automatically for images and scanned PDFs. Tesseract is the default backend (native binding, no external install required).
 272 | 
 273 | ### Backends
 274 | 
 275 | - **Tesseract** (default): Built-in native binding. All Tesseract languages supported.
 276 | - **EasyOCR** (Python only): `pip install kreuzberg[easyocr]`. Pass `easyocr_kwargs={"gpu": True}`.
 277 | - **PaddleOCR** (Python only): `pip install kreuzberg[paddleocr]`. Pass `paddleocr_kwargs={"use_angle_cls": True}`.
 278 | - **Guten** (Node.js only): Built-in OCR backend via `GutenOcrBackend`.
 279 | 
 280 | ### Language Codes
 281 | 
 282 | ```python
 283 | config = ExtractionConfig(ocr=OcrConfig(language="eng"))       # English
 284 | config = ExtractionConfig(ocr=OcrConfig(language="eng+deu"))   # Multiple
 285 | config = ExtractionConfig(ocr=OcrConfig(language="all"))       # All installed
 286 | ```
 287 | 
 288 | ### Force OCR
 289 | 
 290 | ```python
 291 | config = ExtractionConfig(force_ocr=True)  # OCR even if text is extractable
 292 | ```
 293 | 
 294 | ## ExtractionResult Fields
 295 | 
 296 | | Field | Python | Node.js | Rust | Description |
 297 | |-------|--------|---------|------|-------------|
 298 | | Text content | `result.content` | `result.content` | `result.content` | Extracted text (str/String) |
 299 | | MIME type | `result.mime_type` | `result.mimeType` | `result.mime_type` | Input document MIME type |
 300 | | Metadata | `result.metadata` | `result.metadata` | `result.metadata` | Document metadata (dict/object/HashMap) |
 301 | | Tables | `result.tables` | `result.tables` | `result.tables` | Extracted tables with cells + markdown |
 302 | | Languages | `result.detected_languages` | `result.detectedLanguages` | `result.detected_languages` | Detected languages (if enabled) |
 303 | | Chunks | `result.chunks` | `result.chunks` | `result.chunks` | Text chunks (if chunking enabled) |
 304 | | Images | `result.images` | `result.images` | `result.images` | Extracted images (if enabled) |
 305 | | Elements | `result.elements` | `result.elements` | `result.elements` | Semantic elements (if element_based format) |
 306 | | Pages | `result.pages` | `result.pages` | `result.pages` | Per-page content (if page extraction enabled) |
 307 | | Keywords | `result.keywords` | `result.keywords` | `result.keywords` | Extracted keywords (if enabled) |
 308 | 
 309 | ## Error Handling
 310 | 
 311 | ### Python
 312 | 
 313 | ```python
 314 | from kreuzberg import (
 315 |     extract_file_sync, KreuzbergError, ParsingError,
 316 |     OCRError, ValidationError, MissingDependencyError,
 317 | )
 318 | 
 319 | try:
 320 |     result = extract_file_sync("file.pdf")
 321 | except ParsingError as e:
 322 |     print(f"Failed to parse: {e}")
 323 | except OCRError as e:
 324 |     print(f"OCR failed: {e}")
 325 | except ValidationError as e:
 326 |     print(f"Invalid input: {e}")
 327 | except MissingDependencyError as e:
 328 |     print(f"Missing dependency: {e}")
 329 | except KreuzbergError as e:
 330 |     print(f"Extraction failed: {e}")
 331 | ```
 332 | 
 333 | ### Node.js
 334 | 
 335 | ```typescript
 336 | import {
 337 |     extractFile, KreuzbergError, ParsingError,
 338 |     OcrError, ValidationError, MissingDependencyError,
 339 | } from '@kreuzberg/node';
 340 | 
 341 | try {
 342 |     const result = await extractFile('file.pdf');
 343 | } catch (e) {
 344 |     if (e instanceof ParsingError) { /* ... */ }
 345 |     else if (e instanceof OcrError) { /* ... */ }
 346 |     else if (e instanceof ValidationError) { /* ... */ }
 347 |     else if (e instanceof KreuzbergError) { /* ... */ }
 348 | }
 349 | ```
 350 | 
 351 | ### Rust
 352 | 
 353 | ```rust
 354 | use kreuzberg::{extract_file, ExtractionConfig, KreuzbergError};
 355 | 
 356 | let config = ExtractionConfig::default();
 357 | match extract_file("file.pdf", None, &config).await {
 358 |     Ok(result) => println!("{}", result.content),
 359 |     Err(KreuzbergError::Parsing(msg)) => eprintln!("Parse error: {msg}"),
 360 |     Err(KreuzbergError::Ocr(msg)) => eprintln!("OCR error: {msg}"),
 361 |     Err(e) => eprintln!("Error: {e}"),
 362 | }
 363 | ```
 364 | 
 365 | ## Common Pitfalls
 366 | 
 367 | 1. **Python ChunkingConfig fields**: Use `max_chars` and `max_overlap`, NOT `max_characters` or `overlap`.
 368 | 2. **Rust extract_file signature**: Third argument is `&ExtractionConfig` (a reference), not `Option`. Use `&ExtractionConfig::default()` for defaults.
 369 | 3. **Rust feature gates**: `extract_file_sync`, `batch_extract_file`, and `batch_extract_file_sync` all require `features = ["tokio-runtime"]` in Cargo.toml.
 370 | 4. **Rust async context**: `extract_file` is async. Use `#[tokio::main]` or call from an async context.
 371 | 5. **CLI --format vs --output-format**: `--format` controls CLI output (text/json). `--output-format` controls content format (plain/markdown/djot/html).
 372 | 6. **Node.js extractFile signature**: `extractFile(path, mimeType?, config?)` — mimeType is the second arg (pass `null` to skip).
 373 | 7. **Python detect_mime_type**: The function for detecting from bytes is `detect_mime_type(data)`. For paths use `detect_mime_type_from_path(path)`.
 374 | 8. **Config file field names**: Use snake_case in TOML/YAML/JSON config files (e.g., `max_chars`, `max_overlap`, `pdf_options`).
 375 | 
 376 | ## Supported Formats (Summary)
 377 | 
 378 | | Category | Extensions |
 379 | |----------|-----------|
 380 | | **PDF** | `.pdf` |
 381 | | **Word** | `.docx`, `.odt` |
 382 | | **Spreadsheets** | `.xlsx`, `.xlsm`, `.xlsb`, `.xls`, `.xla`, `.xlam`, `.xltm`, `.ods` |
 383 | | **Presentations** | `.pptx`, `.ppt`, `.ppsx` |
 384 | | **eBooks** | `.epub`, `.fb2` |
 385 | | **Images** | `.png`, `.jpg`, `.jpeg`, `.gif`, `.webp`, `.bmp`, `.tiff`, `.tif`, `.jp2`, `.jpx`, `.jpm`, `.mj2`, `.jbig2`, `.jb2`, `.pnm`, `.pbm`, `.pgm`, `.ppm`, `.svg` |
 386 | | **Markup** | `.html`, `.htm`, `.xhtml`, `.xml` |
 387 | | **Data** | `.json`, `.yaml`, `.yml`, `.toml`, `.csv`, `.tsv` |
 388 | | **Text** | `.txt`, `.md`, `.markdown`, `.djot`, `.rst`, `.org`, `.rtf` |
 389 | | **Email** | `.eml`, `.msg` |
 390 | | **Archives** | `.zip`, `.tar`, `.tgz`, `.gz`, `.7z` |
 391 | | **Academic** | `.bib`, `.biblatex`, `.ris`, `.nbib`, `.enw`, `.csl`, `.tex`, `.latex`, `.typ`, `.jats`, `.ipynb`, `.docbook`, `.opml`, `.pod`, `.mdoc`, `.troff` |
 392 | 
 393 | See [references/supported-formats.md](references/supported-formats.md) for the complete format reference with MIME types.

### File: `skills\kreuzberg\references\advanced-features.md`

- Size: 28126 bytes
- Modified: SystemTime { intervals: 134209877266921256 }

```markdown
   1 | # Advanced Features Reference
   2 | 
   3 | Kreuzberg provides powerful advanced features for customization, semantic processing, and integration with external systems.
   4 | 
   5 | ## Plugin System
   6 | 
   7 | The plugin system allows you to extend Kreuzberg's extraction pipeline with custom post-processors, validators, and OCR backends. Plugins run within the extraction pipeline and have direct access to extraction results.
   8 | 
   9 | ### Custom Post-Processors
  10 | 
  11 | Post-processors enrich extraction results after document parsing. They run non-destructively—if a post-processor fails, the extraction succeeds anyway (errors are logged).
  12 | 
  13 | === "Python"
  14 | 
  15 |     ```python
  16 |     from kreuzberg import register_post_processor, ExtractionResult
  17 | 
  18 |     class MetadataEnricher:
  19 |         def name(self) -> str:
  20 |             return "metadata_enricher"
  21 | 
  22 |         def process(self, result: ExtractionResult) -> ExtractionResult:
  23 |             result.metadata["processed_by"] = "metadata_enricher"
  24 |             result.metadata["char_count"] = len(result.content)
  25 |             return result
  26 | 
  27 |         def processing_stage(self) -> str:
  28 |             # "early", "middle", or "late"
  29 |             return "middle"
  30 | 
  31 |         def initialize(self) -> None:
  32 |             print("Initializing metadata enricher")
  33 | 
  34 |         def shutdown(self) -> None:
  35 |             print("Shutting down metadata enricher")
  36 | 
  37 |     register_post_processor(MetadataEnricher())
  38 | 
  39 |     # Now use extraction with the registered processor
  40 |     from kreuzberg import extract_file_sync
  41 |     result = extract_file_sync("document.pdf")
  42 |     print(result.metadata["char_count"])
  43 |     ```
  44 | 
  45 | === "TypeScript"
  46 | 
  47 |     ```typescript
  48 |     import { registerPostProcessor, ExtractionResult } from '@kreuzberg/node';
  49 | 
  50 |     const enricher = {
  51 |         name(): string {
  52 |             return "metadata_enricher";
  53 |         },
  54 | 
  55 |         async process(result: ExtractionResult): Promise<ExtractionResult> {
  56 |             result.metadata.processed_by = "metadata_enricher";
  57 |             result.metadata.char_count = result.content.length;
  58 |             return result;
  59 |         },
  60 | 
  61 |         processingStage?(): "early" | "middle" | "late" {
  62 |             return "middle";
  63 |         },
  64 | 
  65 |         async initialize?(): Promise<void> {
  66 |             console.log("Initializing metadata enricher");
  67 |         },
  68 | 
  69 |         async shutdown?(): Promise<void> {
  70 |             console.log("Shutting down metadata enricher");
  71 |         }
  72 |     };
  73 | 
  74 |     registerPostProcessor(enricher);
  75 | 
  76 |     // Now use extraction with the registered processor
  77 |     const result = await extractFile("document.pdf");
  78 |     console.log(result.metadata.char_count);
  79 |     ```
  80 | 
  81 | ### Custom Validators
  82 | 
  83 | Validators perform quality checks on extraction results. Unlike post-processors, validator failures cause the entire extraction to fail. Use validators to enforce quality standards.
  84 | 
  85 | === "Python"
  86 | 
  87 |     ```python
  88 |     from kreuzberg import register_validator, ExtractionResult, ValidationError
  89 | 
  90 |     class MinimumContentValidator:
  91 |         def name(self) -> str:
  92 |             return "min_content_validator"
  93 | 
  94 |         def validate(self, result: ExtractionResult) -> None:
  95 |             if len(result.content) < 100:
  96 |                 raise ValidationError("Extracted content too short (< 100 chars)")
  97 | 
  98 |         def priority(self) -> int:
  99 |             # Higher priority runs first (0-1000, default 50)
 100 |             return 100
 101 | 
 102 |         def should_validate(self, result: ExtractionResult) -> bool:
 103 |             # Only validate PDFs
 104 |             return "pdf" in result.mime_type.lower()
 105 | 
 106 |         def initialize(self) -> None:
 107 |             pass
 108 | 
 109 |         def shutdown(self) -> None:
 110 |             pass
 111 | 
 112 |     register_validator(MinimumContentValidator())
 113 | 
 114 |     # Extraction will fail if content < 100 chars
 115 |     result = extract_file_sync("document.pdf")
 116 |     ```
 117 | 
 118 | === "TypeScript"
 119 | 
 120 |     ```typescript
 121 |     import { registerValidator, ExtractionResult } from '@kreuzberg/node';
 122 | 
 123 |     const validator = {
 124 |         name(): string {
 125 |             return "min_content_validator";
 126 |         },
 127 | 
 128 |         async validate(result: ExtractionResult): Promise<void> {
 129 |             if (result.content.length < 100) {
 130 |                 throw new Error("Extracted content too short (< 100 chars)");
 131 |             }
 132 |         },
 133 | 
 134 |         priority?(): number {
 135 |             return 100;
 136 |         },
 137 | 
 138 |         shouldValidate?(result: ExtractionResult): boolean {
 139 |             return result.mimeType.toLowerCase().includes("pdf");
 140 |         },
 141 | 
 142 |         async initialize?(): Promise<void> {},
 143 | 
 144 |         async shutdown?(): Promise<void> {}
 145 |     };
 146 | 
 147 |     registerValidator(validator);
 148 | 
 149 |     // Extraction will fail if content < 100 chars
 150 |     const result = await extractFile("document.pdf");
 151 |     ```
 152 | 
 153 | ### Custom OCR Backends
 154 | 
 155 | Implement custom OCR engines by registering an OCR backend. This allows integration with proprietary or specialized OCR solutions.
 156 | 
 157 | === "Python"
 158 | 
 159 |     ```python
 160 |     from kreuzberg import register_ocr_backend
 161 | 
 162 |     class CustomOcrBackend:
 163 |         def name(self) -> str:
 164 |             return "custom_ocr"
 165 | 
 166 |         def supported_languages(self) -> list[str]:
 167 |             return ["eng", "deu", "fra", "spa"]
 168 | 
 169 |         def process_image(self, image_bytes: bytes, language: str) -> dict:
 170 |             # image_bytes: raw image data
 171 |             # language: ISO 639-3 code (e.g., "eng", "deu")
 172 | 
 173 |             # Call your OCR engine here
 174 |             # text = my_ocr_engine.recognize(image_bytes, language)
 175 | 
 176 |             return {
 177 |                 "content": "Extracted text from image",
 178 |                 "metadata": {"confidence": 0.95, "language": language},
 179 |                 "tables": []
 180 |             }
 181 | 
 182 |         def process_file(self, path: str, language: str) -> dict:
 183 |             # Optional: custom file processing
 184 |             # Called when extracting OCR from a file path
 185 |             with open(path, "rb") as f:
 186 |                 image_bytes = f.read()
 187 |             return self.process_image(image_bytes, language)
 188 | 
 189 |         def initialize(self) -> None:
 190 |             # Load models, initialize engine
 191 |             pass
 192 | 
 193 |         def shutdown(self) -> None:
 194 |             # Clean up resources
 195 |             pass
 196 | 
 197 |         def version(self) -> str:
 198 |             return "1.0.0"
 199 | 
 200 |     register_ocr_backend(CustomOcrBackend())
 201 | 
 202 |     # Use in extraction config
 203 |     from kreuzberg import ExtractionConfig, OcrConfig, extract_file_sync
 204 | 
 205 |     config = ExtractionConfig(
 206 |         ocr=OcrConfig(backend="custom_ocr", language="eng")
 207 |     )
 208 |     result = extract_file_sync("scanned.pdf", config=config)
 209 |     ```
 210 | 
 211 | === "TypeScript"
 212 | 
 213 |     ```typescript
 214 |     import { registerOcrBackend, ExtractionConfig, extractFile } from '@kreuzberg/node';
 215 | 
 216 |     const backend = {
 217 |         name(): string {
 218 |             return "custom_ocr";
 219 |         },
 220 | 
 221 |         supportedLanguages(): string[] {
 222 |             return ["eng", "deu", "fra", "spa"];
 223 |         },
 224 | 
 225 |         async processImage(
 226 |             imageBytes: Uint8Array | string,
 227 |             language: string
 228 |         ): Promise<{
 229 |             content: string;
 230 |             mime_type: string;
 231 |             metadata: Record<string, unknown>;
 232 |             tables: unknown[];
 233 |         }> {
 234 |             const buffer = typeof imageBytes === "string"
 235 |                 ? Buffer.from(imageBytes, "base64")
 236 |                 : Buffer.from(imageBytes);
 237 | 
 238 |             // Call your OCR engine
 239 |             // const text = await myOcrEngine.recognize(buffer, language);
 240 | 
 241 |             return {
 242 |                 content: "Extracted text from image",
 243 |                 mime_type: "text/plain",
 244 |                 metadata: { confidence: 0.95, language },
 245 |                 tables: []
 246 |             };
 247 |         },
 248 | 
 249 |         async initialize?(): Promise<void> {
 250 |             // Load models, initialize engine
 251 |         },
 252 | 
 253 |         async shutdown?(): Promise<void> {
 254 |             // Clean up resources
 255 |         }
 256 |     };
 257 | 
 258 |     registerOcrBackend(backend);
 259 | 
 260 |     // Use in extraction config
 261 |     const config: ExtractionConfig = {
 262 |         ocr: { backend: "custom_ocr", language: "eng" }
 263 |     };
 264 |     const result = await extractFile("scanned.pdf", null, config);
 265 |     ```
 266 | 
 267 | ## Per-File Configuration in Batch Operations
 268 | 
 269 | Use `FileExtractionConfig` to override extraction settings for individual files within a batch. This is useful for mixed-format batches where different documents need different OCR, output, or processing settings.
 270 | 
 271 | === "Python"
 272 | 
 273 |     ```python
 274 |     from kreuzberg import (
 275 |         batch_extract_files_sync,
 276 |         ExtractionConfig, FileExtractionConfig, OcrConfig,
 277 |     )
 278 | 
 279 |     config = ExtractionConfig(output_format="markdown")
 280 |     paths = ["report.pdf", "scan.tiff"]
 281 |     file_configs = [
 282 |         None,  # use batch defaults
 283 |         FileExtractionConfig(
 284 |             force_ocr=True,
 285 |             ocr=OcrConfig(backend="tesseract", language="deu"),
 286 |         ),
 287 |     ]
 288 |     results = batch_extract_files_sync(paths, config, file_configs=file_configs)
 289 |     ```
 290 | 
 291 | === "TypeScript"
 292 | 
 293 |     ```typescript
 294 |     import { batchExtractFilesSync } from '@kreuzberg/node';
 295 | 
 296 |     const results = batchExtractFilesSync(
 297 |       ['report.pdf', 'scan.tiff'],
 298 |       { outputFormat: 'markdown' },
 299 |       [null, { forceOcr: true, ocr: { backend: 'tesseract', language: 'deu' } }],
 300 |     );
 301 |     ```
 302 | 
 303 | All `ExtractionConfig` fields except batch-level concerns (`max_concurrent_extractions`, `use_cache`, `acceleration`, `security_limits`) can be overridden. `None`/`null` fields inherit from the batch default.
 304 | 
 305 | ## Embeddings
 306 | 
 307 | Generate vector embeddings for text chunks using ONNX-based models. Embeddings enable semantic search, clustering, and similarity operations on extracted content.
 308 | 
 309 | **Requirements:** ONNX Runtime 1.22.x or later
 310 | 
 311 | === "Python"
 312 | 
 313 |     ```python
 314 |     from kreuzberg import (
 315 |         ExtractionConfig, ChunkingConfig, EmbeddingConfig,
 316 |         EmbeddingModelType, list_embedding_presets,
 317 |         get_embedding_preset, extract_file_sync
 318 |     )
 319 | 
 320 |     # List available embedding presets
 321 |     presets = list_embedding_presets()
 322 |     print(f"Available presets: {presets}")  # ['balanced', 'compact', 'large']
 323 | 
 324 |     # Get details about a preset
 325 |     preset_info = get_embedding_preset("balanced")
 326 |     print(f"Model: {preset_info.model_name}")
 327 |     print(f"Dimensions: {preset_info.dimensions}")
 328 |     print(f"Recommended chunk size: {preset_info.chunk_size}")
 329 | 
 330 |     # Method 1: Use preset (recommended)
 331 |     config = ExtractionConfig(
 332 |         chunking=ChunkingConfig(
 333 |             max_chars=512,
 334 |             max_overlap=100,
 335 |             embedding=EmbeddingConfig(
 336 |                 model=EmbeddingModelType.preset("balanced"),
 337 |                 normalize=True,
 338 |                 batch_size=32
 339 |             )
 340 |         )
 341 |     )
 342 | 
 343 |     # Method 2: Use specific fastembed model
 344 |     config = ExtractionConfig(
 345 |         chunking=ChunkingConfig(
 346 |             embedding=EmbeddingConfig(
 347 |                 model=EmbeddingModelType.fastembed(
 348 |                     model="BAAI/bge-small-en-v1.5",
 349 |                     dimensions=384
 350 |                 ),
 351 |                 normalize=True
 352 |             )
 353 |         )
 354 |     )
 355 | 
 356 |     # Method 3: Use custom ONNX model from HuggingFace
 357 |     config = ExtractionConfig(
 358 |         chunking=ChunkingConfig(
 359 |             embedding=EmbeddingConfig(
 360 |                 model=EmbeddingModelType.custom(
 361 |                     model_id="sentence-transformers/all-MiniLM-L6-v2",
 362 |                     dimensions=384
 363 |                 ),
 364 |                 cache_dir="/path/to/model/cache"
 365 |             )
 366 |         )
 367 |     )
 368 | 
 369 |     result = extract_file_sync("document.pdf", config=config)
 370 | 
 371 |     # Access embeddings in chunks
 372 |     for chunk in result.chunks:
 373 |         embedding = chunk.embedding  # list[float] or None
 374 |         print(f"Chunk: {chunk.content[:50]}...")
 375 |         print(f"Embedding dimensions: {len(embedding) if embedding else 0}")
 376 |     ```
 377 | 
 378 | === "TypeScript"
 379 | 
 380 |     ```typescript
 381 |     import {
 382 |         ExtractionConfig, ChunkingConfig,
 383 |         listEmbeddingPresets, getEmbeddingPreset,
 384 |         extractFile
 385 |     } from '@kreuzberg/node';
 386 | 
 387 |     // List available embedding presets
 388 |     const presets = listEmbeddingPresets();
 389 |     console.log(`Available presets: ${presets}`);  // ['balanced', 'compact', 'large']
 390 | 
 391 |     // Get details about a preset
 392 |     const preset = getEmbeddingPreset("balanced");
 393 |     console.log(`Model: ${preset.modelName}`);
 394 |     console.log(`Dimensions: ${preset.dimensions}`);
 395 |     console.log(`Recommended chunk size: ${preset.chunkSize}`);
 396 | 
 397 |     // Method 1: Use preset (recommended)
 398 |     const config: ExtractionConfig = {
 399 |         chunking: {
 400 |             maxChars: 512,
 401 |             maxOverlap: 100,
 402 |             embedding: {
 403 |                 model: { type: 'preset', name: 'balanced' },
 404 |                 normalize: true,
 405 |                 batchSize: 32
 406 |             }
 407 |         }
 408 |     };
 409 | 
 410 |     // Method 2: Use specific fastembed model
 411 |     const config2: ExtractionConfig = {
 412 |         chunking: {
 413 |             embedding: {
 414 |                 model: {
 415 |                     type: 'fastembed',
 416 |                     model: 'BAAI/bge-small-en-v1.5',
 417 |                     dimensions: 384
 418 |                 },
 419 |                 normalize: true
 420 |             }
 421 |         }
 422 |     };
 423 | 
 424 |     // Method 3: Use custom ONNX model
 425 |     const config3: ExtractionConfig = {
 426 |         chunking: {
 427 |             embedding: {
 428 |                 model: {
 429 |                     type: 'custom',
 430 |                     modelId: 'sentence-transformers/all-MiniLM-L6-v2',
 431 |                     dimensions: 384
 432 |                 },
 433 |                 cacheDir: '/path/to/model/cache'
 434 |             }
 435 |         }
 436 |     };
 437 | 
 438 |     const result = await extractFile("document.pdf", null, config);
 439 | 
 440 |     // Access embeddings in chunks
 441 |     if (result.chunks) {
 442 |         for (const chunk of result.chunks) {
 443 |             const embedding = chunk.embedding;  // number[] | null
 444 |             console.log(`Chunk: ${chunk.content.substring(0, 50)}...`);
 445 |             console.log(`Embedding dimensions: ${embedding?.length ?? 0}`);
 446 |         }
 447 |     }
 448 |     ```
 449 | 
 450 | ## Keyword Extraction
 451 | 
 452 | Extract important keywords and phrases from documents using YAKE (Yet Another Keyword Extractor) or RAKE (Rapid Automatic Keyword Extraction) algorithms.
 453 | 
 454 | === "Python"
 455 | 
 456 |     ```python
 457 |     from kreuzberg import (
 458 |         ExtractionConfig, KeywordConfig, KeywordAlgorithm,
 459 |         YakeParams, RakeParams, extract_file_sync
 460 |     )
 461 | 
 462 |     # YAKE algorithm (unsupervised, good for general use)
 463 |     config = ExtractionConfig(
 464 |         keywords=KeywordConfig(
 465 |             algorithm=KeywordAlgorithm.Yake,
 466 |             max_keywords=15,
 467 |             min_score=0.1,
 468 |             ngram_range=(1, 3),
 469 |             language="en",
 470 |             yake_params=YakeParams(window_size=2)
 471 |         )
 472 |     )
 473 | 
 474 |     # RAKE algorithm (co-occurrence based)
 475 |     config = ExtractionConfig(
 476 |         keywords=KeywordConfig(
 477 |             algorithm=KeywordAlgorithm.Rake,
 478 |             max_keywords=10,
 479 |             min_score=0.0,
 480 |             language="en",
 481 |             rake_params=RakeParams(
 482 |                 min_word_length=3,
 483 |                 max_words_per_phrase=3
 484 |             )
 485 |         )
 486 |     )
 487 | 
 488 |     result = extract_file_sync("document.pdf", config=config)
 489 | 
 490 |     # Access extracted keywords
 491 |     if result.keywords:
 492 |         for keyword in result.keywords:
 493 |             print(f"Text: {keyword.text}")
 494 |             print(f"Score: {keyword.score}")
 495 |             print(f"Algorithm: {keyword.algorithm}")
 496 |     ```
 497 | 
 498 | === "TypeScript"
 499 | 
 500 |     ```typescript
 501 |     import {
 502 |         ExtractionConfig, KeywordConfig,
 503 |         extractFile
 504 |     } from '@kreuzberg/node';
 505 | 
 506 |     // YAKE algorithm
 507 |     const config: ExtractionConfig = {
 508 |         keywords: {
 509 |             algorithm: "yake",
 510 |             maxKeywords: 15,
 511 |             minScore: 0.1,
 512 |             ngramRange: [1, 3],
 513 |             language: "en",
 514 |             yakeParams: {
 515 |                 windowSize: 2
 516 |             }
 517 |         }
 518 |     };
 519 | 
 520 |     // RAKE algorithm
 521 |     const config2: ExtractionConfig = {
 522 |         keywords: {
 523 |             algorithm: "rake",
 524 |             maxKeywords: 10,
 525 |             minScore: 0.0,
 526 |             language: "en",
 527 |             rakeParams: {
 528 |                 minWordLength: 3,
 529 |                 maxWordsPerPhrase: 3
 530 |             }
 531 |         }
 532 |     };
 533 | 
 534 |     const result = await extractFile("document.pdf", null, config);
 535 | 
 536 |     // Access extracted keywords
 537 |     if (result.keywords) {
 538 |         for (const keyword of result.keywords) {
 539 |             console.log(`Text: ${keyword.text}`);
